## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics (batch kinetics / rate laws)
**Analysis**: The target dA_dt is explicitly the time-derivative of a concentration A(t), which is the standard form of ordinary differential equations used to describe reaction rate laws in chemical kinetics. With only t and A available, the most likely relationships are elementary/empirical rate laws (orders in A), possibly with explicit time-dependent rate coefficients (e.g., catalyst deactivation or external forcing).

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order decay (constant-rate consumption): dA_dt = -c0 (rate independent of A; e.g., surface-limited, saturated catalyst)
- First-order decay: dA_dt = -c0 * A (unimolecular decay / radioactive-like kinetics / many elementary steps under pseudo-first-order conditions)
- Second-order decay (single-species): dA_dt = -c0 * A**2 (bimolecular with identical reactants or recombination-like kinetics)
- n-th order power-law: dA_dt = -c0 * A**c1 (empirical rate order not necessarily integer)
- General production/decay with source term: dA_dt = c0 - c1 * A (continuous formation plus first-order loss; approach to steady state)
- Reversible/relaxation-to-equilibrium form: dA_dt = -c0 * (A - c1) (linear relaxation toward equilibrium concentration c1)
- Logistic-like autocatalysis with carrying capacity (bounded growth in A): dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (autocatalytic growth limited by depletion/competition)
- Autocatalysis with baseline initiation: dA_dt = c0 * (A + c1) * (c2 - A) (captures induction/seeded growth without A=0 being absorbing)
- Rational (inhibition/limitation) rate law: dA_dt = -c0 * A / (c1 + A) (effective saturation or self-inhibition with increasing A)
- Rational with higher-order saturation: dA_dt = -c0 * A**c1 / (c2 + A**c1) (sharper transition between low-A and high-A regimes)
- Time-dependent rate coefficient (catalyst decay / changing conditions): dA_dt = -c0 * exp(-c1 * t) * A (effective first-order with decaying k(t))
- Periodic forcing of rate (e.g., light modulation, temperature cycling proxy): dA_dt = -A * (c0 + c1 * sin(c2 * t)) (time-varying first-order consumption)
- Empirical drift + kinetic term: dA_dt = c0 + c1 * t - c2 * A (captures slow baseline drift plus first-order relaxation)
- Stretched-exponential-like effective kinetics (non-ideal/heterogeneous environments): dA_dt = -c0 * t**c1 * A (rate coefficient increases/decreases as a power of time)
- Piecewise-approximable induction without explicit pieces (smooth turn-on): dA_dt = -c0 * A * (1 - exp(-c1 * t)) (reaction turns on gradually due to mixing/activation)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- If dA_dt scales linearly with A over the dataset, expect first-order structure dA_dt ∝ -A; if it scales with A**2, expect second-order.
- If dA_dt is nearly constant while A changes substantially, a zero-order term (-c0) is likely, indicating saturation or surface-limited kinetics.
- A nonzero steady state A* is indicated when dA_dt crosses zero near a constant A value; models like dA_dt = -c0*(A-c1) or dA_dt = c0 - c1*A capture this.
- If |dA_dt| decreases faster than linearly as A grows (self-limiting), rational forms like -A/(c + A) or bounded-growth forms A*(c-A) are plausible.
- If the apparent rate constant changes over time at fixed A (e.g., same A gives different dA_dt at different t), include explicit time dependence such as exp(-c*t), t**c, or sinusoidal modulation in the coefficient multiplying A.
- Autocatalysis is suggested when dA_dt is small at low A but increases as A increases (positive feedback), often captured by dA_dt ∝ A*(c-A) or higher-order A**n terms with n>1 (for growth regimes).
- Induction/mixing delays show as dA_dt ≈ 0 initially then transitioning smoothly; multiplicative turn-on factors like (1 - exp(-c*t)) on a kinetic term can represent this without hard thresholds.
- If dA_dt changes sign as A increases (growth at low A, decay at high A), expect a factorized polynomial structure like A*(c-A) rather than a pure negative power law.
- Strong curvature in dA_dt vs A on log-log plots suggests fractional/empirical reaction order (A**c) rather than integer-order kinetics.

GT: -c0*A**c1 + c2*_q*A*log(c3*t + c4)
Candidate formulas: 52

GT (fixed):  
\[
f(t,A)= -0.1149290460\,A^2 + 0.06806555110\,A\cdot \log(0.2569297861\,t+1)
\]
So any matching candidate must be exactly “(constant)\(A^2\) + (constant)\(A\log(\text{affine in }t)\)” with **no extra** \(A\), \(t\), constants, trig, exp, rational terms, etc. Also the log argument must be \(1+k t\) (or \(1+k|t|\) if we accept a restricted domain like \(t\ge 0\)).

---

### 1. \(A^2c0 + Ac1 + Ac2(c3+t)^{c4}\)
Has an \(A\) linear term and a power term, not \(A\log(\cdot)\). Cannot become \(A\log(1+kt)\). **No**.

### 2. \(A^2c0 + Ac1 + A^{c2}c3\log(c4|c5t|+1)\cos(c6t)\)
Extra \(Ac1\). Also \(\cos(c6t)\) must be identically 1 ⇒ set \(c6=0\). Then need \(A^{c2}\) to be \(A\) ⇒ \(c2=1\). Still stuck with extra \(Ac1\) unless \(c1=0\). Then it can match the structure \(A^2(\cdot)+A\log(1+k|t|)\). Choose \(t\ge 0\) so \(|t|=t\). Yes, can match GT by:
- \(c0=-0.1149290460\)
- \(c1=0\)
- \(c2=1\)
- \(c6=0\)
- \(c3=0.06806555110\)
- \(c4c5=0.2569297861\) (e.g. \(c4=0.2569297861, c5=1\))
**Matches (with domain \(t\ge 0\) if using Abs).**

### 3. \(A^2c0 + A^2c1 + Ac2 + Ac3(c4+t)^{c5}\)
Power term not log; also extra \(Ac2\). **No**.

### 4. Mixed exp/rational/log terms
Can zero out extras, but the remaining log term is \(A^{c7}c8\log(c9|t|+1)\). Set \(c7=1\), kill other terms by setting their coefficients 0, and set \(t\ge 0\). Then it reduces to \(A^2c0 + A\cdot(\text{const})\log(1+kt)\) if we also set \(c1=0\) (to remove \(Ac1\)). So **yes**: pick
- \(c0=-0.1149290460\)
- \(c1=0\)
- set coefficients of exp and rational pieces to 0 (e.g. \(c3=0\), \(c5=0\))
- \(c7=1\), \(c8=0.06806555110\), \(c9=0.2569297861\)
**Matches (with \(t\ge 0\)).**

### 5. \(A^2c0 + A^2c1 + Ac2\log(c3|t|+1)\)
Combine \(A^2\) coefficients: need \(c0+c1=-0.1149290460\). Need \(Ac2\log(1+c3|t|)\) to match; take \(t\ge 0\), set \(c2=0.06806555110\), \(c3=0.2569297861\). **Matches.**

### 6. \(A^2c0 + Ac1\log(c2|t|+1)\)
Exactly the needed form (no extra terms). Take \(t\ge 0\), set \(c0=-0.1149290460\), \(c1=0.06806555110\), \(c2=0.2569297861\). **Matches.**

### 7. \(A^2c0 + Ac1\log(c2|c3t|+1)\)
Same as #6 since \(c2|c3t| = (c2|c3|)|t|\). Take \(t\ge 0\). Choose \(c0=-0.1149290460\), \(c1=0.06806555110\), and \(c2|c3|=0.2569297861\). **Matches.**

### 8–9. Include many extra terms (constants, \(t^{c5}\), logs in \(A\), etc.)
Could set many coefficients to 0, but both have leftover terms unless aggressively zeroed; still can reduce to \(A^2c0 + (\text{something})\cdot |A|\log(1+k|t|)\) in #9 or product of logs in #8. GT needs \(A\log(\cdot)\) only. #9 could set \(c7\neq 0\) and \(c9=1\) to get \(|A|\), but then there is no separate \(A^2\) term unless kept; however the structure becomes \(A^2(\cdot)+|A|\log(\cdot)\), which matches GT on domain \(A\ge 0, t\ge 0\). Yet #9’s log term is \(c7\log(c8|t|+1)|A|^{c9}\): set \(c9=1\), \(A\ge 0\Rightarrow |A|=A\), \(t\ge 0\Rightarrow |t|=t\), and set all other coefficients to 0. Then it becomes \(A^2c0 + c7 A\log(1+c8 t)\). **So #9 matches** (pick \(c0=-0.1149290460\), \(c7=0.06806555110\), \(c8=0.2569297861\), others 0).  
#8 has \(\log(\cdot A)\log(\cdot t)\) product; cannot become single log term unless one log is constant, which would require its argument constant for all \(A\), impossible. **#8 no.**

### 10. \(A^2c0 + Ac1\log(c2|t|+1) + c3 t (A+c4)^{c5}\)
Extra \(t(A+c4)^{c5}\) term; only removable by \(c3=0\). Then reduces to #6 form. **Matches** (with \(c3=0\), \(t\ge 0\)).

### 11. \(A^2c0 + Ac1\log(c2|t|+1) + Ac3(c4+t)^{c5}\)
Extra power term unless \(c3=0\). Then matches like #6. **Matches** (with \(c3=0\), \(t\ge 0\)).

### 12. \(A^2c0 + Ac1\log(\cdot) + Ac3 + Ac4 e^{c5 t}\)
Extra \(Ac3\) and \(Ae^{c5 t}\) unless \(c3=0\) and \(c4=0\). Then matches #6. **Matches**.

### 13. Adds a sine-of-log(exp(A…)) term
